## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: The task describes the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, a classical mechanics problem where the second-order ODE d┬▓x/dt┬▓ = dv/dt is a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The nonlinearity implies restoring forces beyond linear -c0*x, such as polynomial stiffness, nonlinear damping, or periodic driving.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x
- Forced Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3
- Pendulum equation: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x
- Quadratic stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**2 - c2 * v
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * v**3 - c2 * x
- Coulomb friction: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v)
- Forced van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x + c3 * sin(c4 * t)
- Toda oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (exp(c1 * x) - 1) - c2 * v
- Mixed coupling: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x * v
- Asymmetric Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**2 - c2 * x**3 - c3 * v

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope тЖТ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects тЖТ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay тЖТ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior тЖТ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects тЖТ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear restoring force (-c0*x) yields pure harmonic oscillation with frequency proportional to sqrt(c0).
- Cubic stiffness term (-c1*x**3) introduces amplitude-dependent frequency (Duffing nonlinearity).
- Velocity-proportional term (-c1*v) represents viscous damping, causing exponential energy decay.
- Self-sustained (van der Pol) term c0*(1 - c1*x**2)*v provides negative damping for |x|<1, creating a stable limit cycle.
- Explicit periodic time dependence (cos(c4*t) or sin(c4*t)) indicates an external driving force; resonance occurs near natural frequency.
- Asymmetric restoring force (-c1*x**2) breaks symmetry, leading to a non-zero equilibrium offset and even-order harmonic generation.
- Coulomb friction term (-c1*sign(v)) gives constant-magnitude dry friction opposing motion.
- Pendulum-type sin(c1*x) restoring force saturates for large x, making oscillation period increase with amplitude.
- Parametric excitation (coefficient of x as 1 + c1*cos(c2*t)) can cause instability via parametric resonance.
- Nonlinear damping like -c2*v**3 becomes stronger at high velocity, suppressing large-amplitude motions faster.
